The company was co-founded by Chuck Dietzen and Michael Hall. It provides a cloud-based all-in-one EHR, practice management, billing, and telehealth platform primarily for small to mid-sized ambulatory specialty practices. iSALUS was acquired by **EverCommerce** (NYSE: EVCM) in late 2018 and now operates within EverCommerce's **EverHealth** division. In early 2019, EverCommerce also acquired **AllMeds, Inc.** (an EHR vendor for ENT, orthopedics, neurosurgery, and pain management), and in October 2019 formally integrated AllMeds and iSALUS under one organization. This integration led to the launch of **ENTChoice**, a specialty EHR product for otolaryngologists. Michael Hall departed as CEO in August 2020 and was succeeded by Brent Michael as president of the combined healthcare technology division.\n     9→\n    10→The company is relatively small — estimated at 51–62 employees with revenue estimates in the low single-digit millions (though exact figures are uncertain as it reports within EverCommerce). iSALUS claims to serve practices across 48 states and processes nearly half a billion dollars in medical claims annually. It is not a component — the certified module encompasses the entire product. The platform provides a single database and single login for clinical charting, scheduling, billing, e-prescribing, patient portal, telehealth, and administrative functions. The company was co-founded by Chuck Dietzen and Michael Hall. It provides a cloud-based all-in-one EHR, practice management, billing, and telehealth platform primarily for small to mid-sized ambulatory specialty practices. iSALUS was acquired by **EverCommerce** (NYSE: EVCM) in late 2018 and now operates within EverCommerce's **EverHealth** division. In early 2019, EverCommerce also acquired **AllMeds, Inc.** (an EHR vendor for ENT, orthopedics, neurosurgery, and pain management), and in October 2019 formally integrated AllMeds and iSALUS under one organization. This integration led to the launch of **ENTChoice**, a specialty EHR product for otolaryngologists. Michael Hall departed as CEO in August 2020 and was succeeded by Brent Michael as president of the combined healthcare technology division.\n\nThe company is relatively small — estimated at 51–62 employees with revenue estimates in the low single-digit millions (though exact figures are uncertain as it reports within EverCommerce). iSALUS claims to serve practices across 48 states and processes nearly half a billion dollars in medical claims annually. They primarily target private specialty practices, from solo practitioners to groups with 50+ physicians.\n\n## Product: OfficeEMR\n\nCHPL ID: 10914\n\n### What It Is\n\nOfficeEMR is a **full, all-in-one cloud-based EHR, practice management, and billing suite** designed for small and medium-sized ambulatory medical practices. It is not a component — the certified module encompasses the entire product. The platform provides a single database and single login for clinical charting, scheduling, billing, e-prescribing, patient portal, telehealth, and administrative functions. It is entirely web-based (works on any OS) and also has a mobile app (iOS and Android) supporting charge capture, e-prescribing, remote charting, telehealth, and patient image viewing.\n\nThe ONC certification (June 2022) covers 37 criteria spanning clinical data capture (a)(1)–(a)(5), (a)(12), (a)(14), transitions of care (b)(1)–(b)(3), (b)(10)–(b)(11), patient engagement (e)(1), (e)(3), public health reporting (f)(1), (f)(2), (f)(5), standardized API/FHIR (g)(10), and direct messaging (h)(1). This is a comprehensive ambulatory EHR certification.\n\n### Users & Market\n\n**Target users:** Physicians, practice managers, billing staff, and clinical support staff in ambulatory/outpatient settings. Not designed for inpatient or hospital use.\n\n**Specialties:** iSALUS has purpose-built configurations for several core specialties:\n- Nephrology (including a dedicated dialysis rounding feature)\n- Urology\n- Otolaryngology/ENT (via ENTChoice, post-AllMeds integration)\n- Orthopaedics\n- Neurosurgery\n- Pain Management\n\nBeyond these, the platform supports 45+ specialties through its customizable \"Choice EHR\" option, including cardiology, dermatology, family medicine, gastroenterology, OB-Gyn, pediatrics, psychiatry, and many others.\n\n**Practice size:** Solo practices through organizations with 50+ physicians. The free tier suggests they pursue very small practices as an entry point.\n\n**Customer count:** Not publicly disclosed. The company claims \"thousands of healthcare providers\" but no specific numbers are available. A 2012 partnership with St. Vincent Health (Indiana) to offer OfficeEMR to independent physicians throughout Indiana is one of the few named deployments.\n\n**Reviews:** Limited online review presence — Capterra shows a 5.0/5.0 rating but with very few reviews. FindEMR shows 4/5 stars from 3 reviews. No KLAS ratings found. The small review footprint is consistent with a smaller vendor.\n\n### Modules & Functionality\n\nBased on vendor website, help documentation, and third-party profiles, OfficeEMR includes the following integrated modules:\n\n**Clinical / EHR:**\n- Clinical charting with pre-built and customizable templates\n- Progress notes and treatment plans\n- Problem list, allergies, and medication management\n- Vitals recording\n- Clinical reconciliation (auto-post previous medications, allergies, problems)\n- Clinical decision support with customizable alert rules\n- Procedure note templates (surgical documentation including type of surgery, implants/devices, blood loss, postoperative instructions)\n- Specialty-specific dialysis rounding feature (vital signs, treatment details, medications with auto-populated billing codes)\n- Patient image capture and viewing\n- Letters/correspondence generation\n\n**E-Prescribing:**\n- E-prescribing including EPCS (Electronic Prescribing for Controlled Substances)\n- Integration with CoverMyMeds for Real-Time Benefit Checks and Electronic Prior Authorization\n\n**Scheduling:**\n- iScheduler module for appointment management\n- Patient recall with automated appointment reminders\n- Check-in / check-out workflows\n\n**Billing & Revenue Cycle:**\n- Claims management and submission\n- Clearinghouse integration\n- Insurance eligibility verification (batch eligibility)\n- Fee schedule management\n- Integrated payment processing\n- Electronic statements\n- Auto-populated billing codes from clinical documentation\n- MIPS/Meaningful Use reporting\n- Patient cost estimator\n- Optional outsourced billing/RCM services (claimed 98.1% average net collection rate)\n\n**Patient Engagement:**\n- Patient Portal (Personal Health Records for families)\n- Intelligent Intake (digital patient intake forms)\n- Patient surveys and online reputation management\n- Patient communications\n\n**Telehealth:**\n- AnywhereCare telehealth module\n- Remote patient charting\n\n**Document Management:**\n- eDocuments (scanning and document management)\n- Exydoc (document management)\n- RecordSync (records management)\n- Electronic faxing\n\n**Labs & Orders:**\n- E-labs (electronic lab results management)\n- Order entry\n- Electronic referral management with two-way interfaces\n\n**Reporting & Analytics:**\n- Dynamic reporting and custom analytics\n- Quality reporting (MIPS)\n- Public health case reporting (immunization registry, syndromic surveillance, electronic case reporting)\n\n**Interoperability:**\n- CCDA exports\n- EHI Export (single patient and all-patient)\n- HL7 interface mappings\n- FHIR API (g)(10) certified\n- Direct messaging (h)(1)\n- InfoDive data extract\n\n**Additional Services (through iSALUS, not strictly part of OfficeEMR software):**\n- Remote Patient Monitoring (RPM)\n- Chronic Care Management (CCM)\n\n### Data & Content\n\nBased on vendor documentation (particularly the EHI Export feature documentation and knowledge base), OfficeEMR stores data across these documented categories:\n\n- **Demographics** — patient demographic information\n- **Insurance** — insurance policy details\n- **Responsible Parties** — responsible party/guarantor records\n- **Payer** — insurance payer information\n- **Appointments** — scheduling data\n- **Authorizations** — referral/authorization records\n- **Emergency Contacts** — patient emergency contact details\n- **Patient Comments** — notes/comments about patients\n- **Vitals** — vital signs measurements\n- **Allergies** — allergy records\n- **Problem List** — clinical problem lists\n- **Prescriptions** — medication prescription data\n- **Progress Notes** — clinical documentation\n- **Letters** — patient correspondence\n- **eDocument Metadata** — metadata for scanned/uploaded documents\n- **Patient Communications** — messages and communications\n- **Fee Schedule** — billing fee information\n- **Claims** — complete claims data\n- **Claim Procedure Lines** — procedure-level claim details\n- **Payments** — payment transaction records\n\nThis list comes from the EHI export documentation itself. The product's feature set suggests additional data domains that may or may not appear in the export — for example, lab results, orders, referrals, immunizations, procedure notes, clinical decision support rules, and patient portal activity are all described as features but are not explicitly listed as separate EHI export categories above. Whether these are subsumed under existing categories (e.g., lab results within progress notes) or potentially missing from the export will need to be evaluated in Phase 2.\n\nThe vendor's billing feature set (claims, clearinghouse integration, eligibility verification, payments, statements, fee schedules) indicates substantial financial data is stored. The telehealth module (AnywhereCare) likely stores visit records. The Intelligent Intake feature stores patient-submitted forms. Document management (eDocuments, Exydoc) stores scanned documents and metadata. The degree to which all of these are captured in the EHI export is a key question for Phase 2.\n\n### Pricing\n\nOfficeEMR uses a tiered pricing model:\n- **Free:** Cloud EHR, appointments, chart notes, e-prescribing, e-labs, 2 hours training\n- **Standard:** Adds billing, scheduling, clearinghouse, 8 hours training\n- **Premium:** Unlimited claims, 20 hours training\n- **Outsourced Billing:** Available as a separate service\n\nExact pricing is not publicly disclosed.\n","numLines":155,"startLine":1,"totalLines":155}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0123Efj2YRMgsk9GnzS8S7t4","type":"tool_result","content":"Overview of EHI Export Overview of EHI Export Tool EHI Exports have been added to OfficeEMR in compliance with ONC requirements to produce both single patient EHI export and entire patient population EHI export. Access to these exports is based on user roles (permissions), and the computable format we use for these exports is JSON. The single patient EHI export functionality requires that users &nbsp;have the ability to export a single patient with the assistance of a software developer. The export must be created in a reasonable time and include all available patient EHI in an electronic and computable format. OfficeEMR users with the appropriate assigned role can do this via the Reports portal EHI Export tool. The export is produced and available to the user for immediate download/save to whatever location or media the practice chooses. Similarly, all patients export functionality must include all available patient population EHI, be exported in an electronic and computable format, but this EHI export can involve additional action by your EMR vendor. The reason is that exporting large volumes of data involves more time, resources, and expense. OfficeEMR users with the appropriate assigned role can submit requests for an all-patient export via the same Reports portal EHI Export tool. The export is produced and provided to the practice by our Data Export team. As part of this ONC requirement, we provide this publicly accessible hyperlink which defines the export &rsquo;s format. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01NmvxW8LmcfMHeAhZg1SeNU","type":"tool_result","content":"EHI Export\nLast Modified on 12/19/2025 8:58 am EST\n\nOverview of EHI Export\n\nOverview of EHI Export Tool\nEHI Exports have been added to OfficeEMR in compliance with ONC requirements to produce both single\npatient EHI export and entire patient population EHI export. Access to these exports is based on user roles\n(permissions), and the computable format we use for these exports is JSON.\nThe single patient EHI export functionality requires that users have the ability to export a single patient with the\nassistance of a software developer. The export must be created in a reasonable time and include all available\npatient EHI in an electronic and computable format. OfficeEMR users with the appropriate assigned role can do\nthis via the Reports portal EHI Export tool. The export is produced and available to the user for immediate\ndownload/save to whatever location or media the practice chooses.\nSimilarly, all patients export functionality must include all available patient population EHI, be exported in an\nelectronic and computable format, but this EHI export can involve additional action by your EMR vendor. The\nreason is that exporting large volumes of data involves more time, resources, and expense. OfficeEMR users\nwith the appropriate assigned role can submit requests for an all-patient export via the same Reports portal EHI\nExport tool. The export is produced and provided to the practice by our Data Export team.\nAs part of this ONC requirement, we provide this publicly accessible hyperlink which defines the export’s format.\nYou can review the articles listed below for details on how to perform both export types, and other information\nrelated to EHI Exports.\n\nPurpose of EHI Export\nAs part of the 21st Century Cures Act, Office EMR will support a new ONC Certification criterion § 170.315 (b)\n(10) Electronic Health Information export. This criterion replaces and expands upon our existing certified\n§170.315(b)(6) Data export which allows our customers to bulk export patient CCDA files.\nThis new Electronic Health Information (EHI) export supports CMS' desire for a patient's and practice's data to\nbe available outside of the platform.\nExcludes: psychotherapy notes (etc)\nRestrict user access by role\nFormat: electronic, computable\nPublicly accessible hyperlink of the export's format included in file\n\n\f§ 170.315 (b)(10) Electronic Health Information export1. Single patient electronic health information export.\n2. Enable a user to timely create an export file(s) with all of a single patient’s electronic health information\nthat can be stored at the time of certification by the product, of which the Health IT Module is a part.\n2. A user must be able to execute this capability at any time the user chooses and\nwithout subsequent developer assistance to operate.\n3. Limit the ability of users who can create such export file(s) in at least one of these two ways:\n1. To a specific set of identified users\n2. As system administrator function.\n4. The export file(s) created must be electronic and in a computable format.\n5. The publicly accessible hyperlink of the export’s format must be included with the exported file(s).\n2. Patient population electronic health information export. Create an export of all the electronic health\ninformation that can be stored at the time of certification by the product, of which the Health IT Module is\na part.\n1. The export created must be electronic and in a computable format.\n2. The publicly accessible hyperlink of the export’s format must be included with the exported file(s).\n3. Documentation. The export format(s) used to support paragraphs (b)(10)(i) and (ii) of this section must\nbe kept up-to-date.\n\nEHI Export Settings\n\nRequired Setup to Perform EHI Exports\nThe ONC requirement for EHI Exports includes the need to restrict which practice users have access to perform\nEHI setup. Therefore, we have created two additional user roles to allow practices to control access to EHI\nExports. EHI Export is the role for users to perform Single Patient exports and EHI Practice Export role\nassignment would allow the user to request an All Patient (Practice) export.\nYou will find details on roles by clicking these links to review Overview of Roles or Assign a Role to a User.\n\n\fSingle Patient Export Role:\n\nPractice (All Patient) Export Role:\n\nAccessing EHI Export\n\nAccessing EHI Export Tool\n\n\fTo access the EHI Export tool, users will go to the Reports portal and then select EHI Export found under the\nGeneral section header. This will open the EHI Export Dashboard where users can see Active requests (within\nthe last 30 days) for both single and all patient requests, and Inactive requests which provides a historical list of\npreviously processed requests (or expired because they are 30+ days old).\nYou can learn more about the exports by clicking on Details for Single Patient Exports or Details for Practice (All\nPatient) Exports.\n\nEHI Export for Single Patient\n\nPerforming an EHI Export for a Single Patient\nFirst you will need to be in the EHI Export screen, and then:\n1. In the EHI Export Screen click on the New Export Request button\n2. Choose Single Patient\n3. Search for your patient by Name or Chart#\n4. Click on Request to build the exported data\n5. You will notice a new entry into your EHI Export Dashboard that begins in a Queued status\n6. Once the export is ready, you will see the status change to Completed\n7. In the Completed status, you have the ability to Download the exported patient data or you can Delete the\nexport that was created (which removes the export from your Active tab of your EHI Export Dashboard and\nmoves it to the Inactive tab)\n\n\f\fEHI Export for Practice (All Patients)\n\nPerforming an EHI Export for your Practice (All\nPatients)\nFirst you will need to be in the EHI Export screen, and then:\n1. In the EHI Export Screen click on the New Export Request button\n2. Choose All Patients\n3. Click Request\n4. Read the Confirmation message that explains the purpose of this All Patient export is to provide you with\nyour patient data because you are planning to leave OfficeEMR and migrating to a new EHR platform.\nClicking 'No' cancels the request and no further action is needing. Clicking 'Yes' will take you to an\nOfficeEMR Data Export Form to gather details for our Data Export Team to process your request for All\nPatient data.\n5. Click the Start button to provide our Data Export Team with your practice details and other information to\nprocess your request to terminate your iSalus Healthcare Services and Export All Patient data.\n6. The final screen in the Data Export Form requests a date you need the export by (please keep in mind the\ntime to deliver data can vary based on practice size but generally we can deliver practice data within 15\ndays of an official request) and the be sure to click on the Submit button because that is how our team is\nnotified of your request.\n\n\f\fAll Patient EHI Export Process Information\n\nProcess Information for All Patient EHI Exports\nWhen practices decide that they want to leave OfficeEMR and switch to a new EHR platform, the All Patient\nExport provides the practice with their patient data in a machine readable format for the consumption of\nanother EHR platform. Based on ONC regulations, charges for All Patient exports are very limited in scope when\nthe request is for practice moving to a new EHR platform. We have outlined our process for All Patient EHI\nExports below so that you have a general idea of what is provided at no-cost, what will incur a cost, how we\ndetermine the time and method of data delivery, and other details specific to your practice. If you have\nquestions that are not answered below, please reach out to our support team to get the answers you are\nseeking.\n\nEHI Export Format Defined\n\nNaming Convention for Data Exports\nAll data export files follow a consistent naming convention:\nPrefix:\n\nFilename that relates to data type being exported\n\nExtension:\n\njson\n\nExample:\n\nallergy.json\n\nFile Structure\nOur exports of system data will be in JSON format and an example of the structure can be found here. The\nsections below for Clinical Data Exports and Practice Management Exports define each data category as a\nnamed export and then details each data element included. You can find an Excel version of these data exports\nhere. Finally, document image data is provided in a separate zipped file with the document image data in its\noriginal format (e.g., PDF, JPEG, PNG, etc.).\n\nUsage and Integration\nFields contained within each export data file are detailed in our public documentation. Each export file will\ncontain the field ‘patientId’ to identify the unique patient that the data pertains to. Access to these exports is based on user roles\n(permissions), and the computable format we use for these exports is JSON.\nThe single patient EHI export functionality requires that users have the ability to export a single patient with the\nassistance of a software developer. This criterion replaces and expands upon our existing certified\n§170.315(b)(6) Data export which allows our customers to bulk export patient CCDA files.\nThis new Electronic Health Information (EHI) export supports CMS' desire for a patient's and practice's data to\nbe available outside of the platform.\nExcludes: psychotherapy notes (etc)\nRestrict user access by role\nFormat: electronic, computable\nPublicly accessible hyperlink of the export's format included in file\n\n\f§ 170.315 (b)(10) Electronic Health Information export1. Single patient electronic health information export.\n2. Enable a user to timely create an export file(s) with all of a single patient’s electronic health information\nthat can be stored at the time of certification by the product, of which the Health IT Module is a part.\n2. Limit the ability of users who can create such export file(s) in at least one of these two ways:\n1. To a specific set of identified users\n2. As system administrator function.\n4. Marked \"COMING SOON: HT1 Release Date is TBD (Q1 2026)\".\n- Individual export category pages (/help/demographics-export, /help/data-export-claims-export, etc.) are part of a separate \"Data Export\" (InfoDive) section for a legacy CSV export tool, not the (b)(10) EHI export. These are distinct from the EHI Export documentation.\n\n## What Was Found\n\n### Export Format\nThe EHI export uses a **proprietary JSON format** — not FHIR, C-CDA, or any other healthcare standard. The export consists of individual JSON files, one per data entity type, following a naming convention of `{entity_name}.json`. Each file contains a JSON array of objects representing records for that patient (single-patient export) or all patients (practice-wide export).\n\nA `readme.json` file is included in every export containing a link back to the publicly accessible format documentation.\n\n### Export Mechanism\n- **Single patient export**: Users with the \"EHI Export\" role can access the EHI Export tool via Reports portal. They search for a patient, request the export, and download a ZIP file once the status changes to \"Completed\". This is self-service and immediate.\n- **All patients (practice) export**: Users with the \"EHI Practice Export\" role submit a request through the same tool. This triggers a process involving the iSALUS Data Export team. The export is described as being for practices migrating to a new EHR platform. Delivery takes approximately 15 days.\n\n### Downloadable Artifacts\nThree outstanding computable artifacts were provided:\n\n1. **JSON Schema files (80 files)**: JSON Schema draft-07 definitions for each export entity. Every field has a property name and type, but all `description` fields are empty strings (`\"\"`). Entity types include clinical data (allergies, vitals, medications, immunizations, lab results, progress notes, etc.) and practice management data (claims, payments, insurance, statements, denials, etc.).\n\n2. **Excel data dictionary (XLSX)**: A single spreadsheet (`iSalus_EHI_ExportDataElements_published_version1_Oct2023_pristine.xlsx`) containing field-level definitions with descriptions.\n\n3. **Sample patient export (58 JSON files)**: A complete export for a test patient (ID 311322), demonstrating the actual export output with realistic test data. This includes claims, appointments, medications, progress notes, template encounters, vitals, lab results, and more.\n\n### Data Dictionary Structure\nThe PDF documentation organizes the data dictionary into two sections:\n\n**Clinical Data Exports** — including: accident, allergy, allergy_symptom, appointment, care_plan_goal, care_team, case_management, case_management_ckcc_note, chart_share (and related sub-files), chronic_care_management, ckcc_status, comment, communication, communication_recipient, consent, demographics, dialysis_setup, dialysis_visit, education, emergency_contact, epa (electronic prior authorization), extension_encounter, extension_results, goal (and sub-files), health_concern, hie, image_document, image_xref, immunization, immunization_registry, implantable_device, insurance, lab_result, letter, md_revolution_status, medication, optimize_rx, order, order_finding, pharmacy, phone_encounter, portal_message, pregnancy, pregnancy_visit, problem_list, problem_list_note, progress_note, referral_tracking, responsible_party, template_encounter (and sub-files for assessment, exam, history, hpi, order_fulfillment, ros, treatment_plan), vital\n\n**Practice Management Data Exports** — including: claim, claim_procedure, denial, eligibility, fee_schedule (referenced but not in schema ZIP), payment, preschool_billing, price_estimate, price_estimate_line, prior_authorization (and sub-files), sliding_fee, statement\n\nEach entry in the data dictionary provides: Export Name (filename), FIELD (field name), and Description (plain-English description of the field's purpose).\n\n## Export Coverage Assessment\n\n### Data Domain Coverage\n\niSALUS has done genuine (b)(10) work here. This is **not** a repackaged FHIR/g(10) API — it is a purpose-built JSON export that covers data well beyond the USCDI clinical subset. The coverage is notably broad for a small vendor:\n\n**Clearly covered domains:**\n- Patient demographics (comprehensive: name, address, phones, identifiers, race, ethnicity, language, employment, marital status, employer, multiple ID types)\n- Insurance and payer information (detailed: 4+ pages of insurance schema fields)\n- Responsible parties / guarantors\n- Appointments and scheduling\n- Allergies and allergy symptoms\n- Problem lists with notes\n- Medications/prescriptions\n- Progress notes\n- Template encounters (with granular sub-files for HPI, ROS, exam, history, assessment, treatment plan, order fulfillment)\n- Vitals (exceptionally detailed: sitting/standing/supine BP, multiple body measurements, pulse ox details)\n- Immunizations and immunization registry data\n- Lab results and orders\n- Letters and correspondence\n- Document metadata (image_document, image_xref) — note: actual document images provided separately as original files (PDF, JPEG, PNG)\n- Patient communications and portal messages\n- Emergency contacts\n- Claims (comprehensive billing data: claim status, charges, balance, aging, providers, payers)\n- Claim procedure lines\n- Payments\n- Denials\n- Statements (with aging buckets)\n- Prior authorizations (with codes and rendering providers)\n- Price estimates\n- Fee schedules\n- Eligibility verification records\n- Consent records\n- Care plans and goals\n- Care teams\n- Health concerns\n- Referral tracking\n- Phone encounters\n- Education records\n- Implantable devices\n- Chronic care management records\n- Dialysis setup and visit data (specialty-specific)\n- Case management and CKCC notes (specialty-specific)\n- Chart sharing records\n- HIE (Health Information Exchange) data\n- EPA (Electronic Prior Authorization) records\n- Sliding fee schedules\n- Preschool billing\n\n**Domains that may be missing or unclear:**\n- **Audit logs / access history**: No schema file for system audit trails or user access logs.\n- **Telehealth session records**: The AnywhereCare telehealth module is a product feature, but no dedicated telehealth visit entity appears in the export. These may be captured within progress_note or template_encounter.\n- **Intelligent Intake (patient intake forms)**: The digital intake module stores patient-submitted forms, but no dedicated schema for intake form data appears.\n- **Patient portal activity**: portal_message is covered, but broader portal interaction logs are not explicitly mentioned.\n- **Clinical decision support rules/alerts**: These are system configuration data and may not be patient-specific EHI.\n- **E-fax records**: Electronic faxing is a product feature but no dedicated fax entity in the export.\n- **MIPS/quality measure data**: Referenced as a product feature but no dedicated export entity.\n- **RPM (Remote Patient Monitoring)**: The md_revolution_status entity appears related but the coverage is unclear.\n- **Custom template data**: Template encounters are well-covered, but whether all custom/specialty-specific template data is fully captured in the generic template_encounter structure is uncertain.\n\n### Export Format & Standards\n\n- **Format**: Proprietary JSON — one file per entity type, each containing a JSON array of record objects.\n- **Standard compliance**: This is not FHIR, C-CDA, or any recognized healthcare data standard. It is a vendor-specific flat data model.\n- **Relationships**: Entities are linked via `patientId` (present in every file). Some entities have foreign keys to others (e.g., `claimId` in claim_procedure links to claim). However, relationship documentation is limited — the data dictionary describes fields but does not formally document entity relationships or cardinality. The PDF mentions some relationships in passing (e.g., \"price_estimate_line.json can be 1-to-many\" relative to price_estimate).\n- **Appropriateness**: For a practice management + ambulatory EHR system, a flat JSON export is a reasonable approach. The vendor-specific format means a receiving system would need custom import logic, but the data structure is straightforward and self-documenting through the JSON Schema and sample export.\n- **Reconstructability**: A third party could reconstruct the patient record from this export. The combination of demographic, clinical, and billing data provides a comprehensive picture. The main challenge would be understanding coded values (e.g., what do specific `claimStatus` values mean?) and reconstructing relationships between template_encounter sub-files.\n\n### Documentation Quality\n\n**Strengths:**\n- **Three complementary artifacts**: JSON Schema files provide machine-readable structure, the XLSX provides human-readable field descriptions, and the sample export demonstrates real output. This is unusually thorough for a vendor of this size.\n- **Comprehensive data dictionary**: The 56-page PDF includes field-level descriptions for every data element across all export entities. Each field has a plain-English description explaining its purpose.\n- **Clear user instructions**: Step-by-step instructions for both single-patient and all-patient exports, including role requirements and process details.\n- **Sample data**: A full single-patient sample export with realistic test data across 58 entity files. This is one of the better artifacts — a developer could immediately understand the format.\n- **Public accessibility**: All documentation is fully public, no login required, hosted on a well-organized KnowledgeOwl knowledge base.\n- **Active maintenance**: Page was last modified 12/19/2025 and HTI-1 updates are already being documented for Q1 2026.\n\n**Weaknesses:**\n- **Empty JSON Schema descriptions**: All `description` fields in the JSON Schema files are empty strings. The schema files define structure and types but provide no semantic context. A developer would need the XLSX or PDF to understand what fields mean.\n- **No value set documentation**: Coded fields (e.g., `claimStatus`, `gender`, `maritalStatus`, `employmentStatus`, `agingType`) are typed as strings but there is no documentation of valid values, code systems, or enumeration sets.\n- **Minimal relationship documentation**: Entity relationships are mostly implicit through shared IDs. No entity-relationship diagram or formal relationship documentation is provided.\n- **No versioning/changelog**: The artifacts are labeled \"v1-OCT2023\" but there's no formal change log documenting what changed between versions.\n- **Date format inconsistency**: Some dates appear as \"YYYYMMDD\" strings (e.g., `birthDate: \"19011212\"`), others as ISO-like formats (e.g., `authorLogDateUtc: \"20150302144846-0400\"`). The documentation does not specify date format conventions.\n\n### Structure & Completeness\n\n- **Granularity**: Field-level documentation with descriptions, though no data type detail beyond JSON Schema types (string, number, object, array). Notably, many nullable fields are typed as `\"type\": \"object\"` rather than using JSON Schema's nullable patterns — this is technically incorrect but understandable.\n- **Entity count**: 80 JSON Schema files covering approximately 70 distinct data entities (excluding readme and sub-entity files).\n- **Sample data coverage**: The sample export includes 58 files, which is fewer than the 80 schema files. Entities present in the schema but absent from the sample (e.g., fee_schedule, sliding_fee, statement, eligibility, hie, immunization_registry, implantable_device, chart_share_detail_*, goal sub-files, health_concern, portal_message) may simply have no data for the test patient.\n- **Coded values**: Not documented. This is the most significant gap — without value sets, a consumer cannot interpret many fields.\n- **Cardinality**: Not formally documented. Implied by the array structure (each file is an array of records).\n\n## Access Summary\n- Final URL (after redirects): https://officeemr.knowledgeowl.com/help/ehi-export\n- Status: found\n- Required browser: no (all content accessible via curl; browser useful for expanding accordions and PDF download)\n- Navigation complexity: direct_link (all downloadable artifacts are linked directly from the main page)\n- Anti-bot issues: none\n\n## Obstacles & Dead Ends\n- The KnowledgeOwl page uses accordion sections that require clicking to expand. This triggers a process involving the iSALUS Data Export team. The export is described as being for practices migrating to a new EHR platform.
